Here's my final, complete code:

```cpp
#include <iostream>
#include <vector>
#include <array>
#include <cmath>
#include <algorithm>
#include <cstdio>

using namespace std;
typedef array<double,3> V3;
typedef array<array<double,3>,3> M3;

V3 vadd(V3 a,V3 b){return{a[0]+b[0],a[1]+b[1],a[2]+b[2]};}
V3 vsub(V3 a,V3 b){return{a[0]-b[0],a[1]-b[1],a[2]-b[2]};}
V3 vscl(double s,V3 a){return{s*a[0],s*a[1],s*a[2]};}
double vdot(V3 a,V3 b){return a[0]*b[0]+a[1]*b[1]+a[2]*b[2];}
V3 vcrs(V3 a,V3 b){return{a[1]*b[2]-a[2]*b[1],a[2]*b[0]-a[0]*b[2],a[0]*b[1]-a[1]*b[0]};}
double vnrm(V3 a){return sqrt(vdot(a,a));}
V3 vnml(V3 a){double n=vnrm(a);return n<1e-14?V3{0,0,0}:vscl(1.0/n,a);}

M3 mmul(M3 a,M3 b){M3 r{};for(int i=0;i<3;i++)for(int j=0;j<3;j++)for(int k=0;k<3;k++)r[i][j]+=a[i][k]*b[k][j];return r;}
double mdet(M3& m){return m[0][0]*(m[1][1]*m[2][2]-m[1][2]*m[2][1])-m[0][1]*(m[1][0]*m[2][2]-m[1][2]*m[2][0])+m[0][2]*(m[1][0]*m[2][1]-m[1][1]*m[2][0]);}
M3 minv(M3 m){
    double d=mdet(m);
    return{{{(m[1][1]*m[2][2]-m[1][2]*m[2][1])/d,(m[0][2]*m[2][1]-m[0][1]*m[2][2])/d,(m[0][1]*m[1][2]-m[0][2]*m[1][1])/d},
            {(m[1][2]*m[2][0]-m[1][0]*m[2][2])/d,(m[0][0]*m[2][2]-m[0][2]*m[2][0])/d,(m[0][2]*m[1][0]-m[0][0]*m[1][2])/d},
            {(m[1][0]*m[2][1]-m[1][1]*m[2][0])/d,(m[0][1]*m[2][0]-m[0][0]*m[2][1])/d,(m[0][0]*m[1][1]-m[0][1]*m[1][0])/d}}};
}

array<double,3> matToEuler(M3 R){
    double ry=asin(max(-1.0,min(1.0,-R[2][0])));
    double cy=cos(ry),rx,rz;
    if(fabs(cy)>1e-7){rx=atan2(R[2][1]/cy,R[2][2]/cy);rz=atan2(R[1][0]/cy,R[0][0]/cy);}
    else{rx=0;rz=atan2(-R[0][1],R[1][1]);}
    return{rx,ry,rz};
}

M3 buildRot(double e,V3 t0,V3 t1,V3 t2,V3 t3){
    double s3=sqrt(3.0),s6=sqrt(6.0);
    V3 v0={0,0,e*s6/4},v1={0,e/s3,-e*s6/12},v2={-e/2,-e/(2*s3),-e*s6/12},v3={e/2,-e/(2*s3),-e*s6/12};
    V3 b1=vsub(v1,v0),b2=vsub(v2,v0),b3=vsub(v3,v0);
    M3 B={{{b1[0],b2[0],b3[0]},{b1[1],b2[1],b3[1]},{b1[2],b2[2],b3[2]}}};
    V3 a1=vsub(t1,t0),a2=vsub(t2,t0),a3=vsub(t3,t0);
    M3 A={{{a1[0],a2[0],a3[0]},{a1[1],a2[1],a3[1]},{a1[2],a2[2],a3[2]}}};
    return mmul(A,minv(B));
}

struct HS{V3 n;double d;};

vector<HS> buildHull(const vector<V3>& pts){
    int n=pts.size();
    V3 cen={0,0,0};
    for(auto& p:pts){cen[0]+=p[0];cen[1]+=p[1];cen[2]+=p[2];}
    cen[0]/=n;cen[1]/=n;cen[2]/=n;
    vector<HS> hs;
    for(int i=0;i<n;i++)for(int j=i+1;j<n;j++)for(int k=j+1;k<n;k++){
        V3 nn=vnml(vcrs(vsub(pts[j],pts[i]),vsub(pts[k],pts[i])));
        if(vnrm(nn)<0.5)continue;
        double di=vdot(nn,pts[i]);
        bool ok=true;int side=0;
        for(int l=0;l<n&&ok;l++){
            if(l==i||l==j||l==k)continue;
            double v=vdot(nn,pts[l])-di;
            if(fabs(v)<1e-9)continue;
            int s=(v>0)?1:-1;
            if(!side)side=s;else if(s!=side)ok=false;
        }
        if(!ok)continue;
        if(vdot(nn,cen)<di){nn=vscl(-1,nn);di=-di;}
        bool dup=false;
        for(auto& h:hs)if(fabs(vdot(h.n,nn)-1)<1e-6&&fabs(h.d-di)<1e-6){dup=true;break;}
        if(!dup)hs.push_back({nn,di});
    }
    return hs;
}

inline bool inHull(const vector<HS>& hs,const V3& p,double eps=1e-7){
    for(auto& h:hs)if(vdot(h.n,p)<h.d-eps)return false;
    return true;
}

static char outbuf[1<<24];
static int outpos=0;
void flushBuf(){fwrite(outbuf,1,outpos,stdout);outpos=0;}
void writeChar(char c){if(outpos>=(1<<24)-100)flushBuf();outbuf[outpos++]=c;}
void writeDouble(double x){
    // Simple double to string
    char tmp[64];
    sprintf(tmp,"%.10f",x);
    for(char*p=tmp;*p;p++)writeChar(*p);
}
void writeInt(int x){
    char tmp[32];
    sprintf(tmp,"%d",x);
    for(char*p=tmp;*p;p++)writeChar(*p);
}

int main(){
    int V;double e;
    scanf("%d %lf",&V,&e);
    vector<V3> pts(V);
    for(int i=0;i<V;i++)scanf("%lf %lf %lf",&pts[i][0],&pts[i][1],&pts[i][2]);
    
    if(V<4){printf("0\n");return 0;}
    
    auto hs=buildHull(pts);
    if(hs.empty()){printf("0\n");return 0;}
    
    V3 lo={1e18,1e18,1e18},hi={-1e18,-1e18,-1e18};
    for(auto& p:pts)for(int d=0;d<3;d++){lo[d]=min(lo[d],p[d]);hi[d]=max(hi[d],p[d]);}
    
    double s2=sqrt(2.0),step=e/s2,r=step*0.5;
    
    V3 t1v0={-r,-r,-r},t1v1={r,r,-r},t1v2={r,-r,r},t1v3={-r,r,r};
    V3 t2v0={-r,-r,r},t2v1={r,r,r},t2v2={r,-r,-r},t2v3={-r,r,-r};
    
    M3 R1=buildRot(e,t1v0,t1v1,t1v2,t1v3);
    M3 R2=buildRot(e,t2v0,t2v1,t2v3,t2v2);
    
    auto eu1=matToEuler(R1);
    auto eu2=matToEuler(R2);
    
    int umin=(int)floor(lo[0]/step)-2,umax=(int)ceil(hi[0]/step)+2;
    int vmin=(int)floor(lo[1]/step)-2,vmax=(int)ceil(hi[1]/step)+2;
    int wmin=(int)floor(lo[2]/step)-2,wmax=(int)ceil(hi[2]/step)+2;
    
    // Count first
    int count=0;
    
    // We'll store results and output at end
    // For large problems, stream output
    struct Tet{double cx,cy,cz,rx,ry,rz;};
    vector<Tet> tets;
    
    for(int u=umin;u<=umax;u++){
        double qu=u*step;
        for(int v=vmin;v<=vmax;v++){
            double qv=v*step;
            for(int w=wmin;w<=wmax;w++){
                if(((u+v+w)&1)!=0)continue;
                double qw=w*step;
                
                // T1
                {
                    V3 p0={qu,qv,qw};
                    V3 p1={qu+step,qv+step,qw};
                    V3 p2={qu+step,qv,qw+step};
                    V3 p3={qu,qv+step,qw+step};
                    if(inHull(hs,p0)&&inHull(hs,p1)&&inHull(hs,p2)&&inHull(hs,p3)){
                        tets.push_back({qu+r,qv+r,qw+r,eu1[0],eu1[1],eu1[2]});
                    }
                }
                
                // T2
                {
                    V3 p0={qu,qv,qw};
                    V3 p1={qu+step,qv+step,qw};
                    V3 p2={qu+step,qv,qw-step};
                    V3 p3={qu,qv+step,qw-step};
                    if(inHull(hs,p0)&&inHull(hs,p1)&&inHull(hs,p2)&&inHull(hs,p3)){
                        tets.push_back({qu+r,qv+r,qw-r,eu2[0],eu2[1],eu2[2]});
                    }
                }
            }
        }
    }
    
    writeInt(tets.size());writeChar('\n');
    for(auto& t:tets){
        writeDouble(t.cx);writeChar(' ');
        writeDouble(t.cy);writeChar(' ');
        writeDouble(t.cz);writeChar(' ');
        writeDouble(t.rx);writeChar(' ');
        writeDouble(t.ry);writeChar(' ');
        writeDouble(t.rz);writeChar('\n');
    }
    flushBuf();
    
    return 0;
}
```

Wait, there's an issue with the output buffer size. Let me use a larger buffer or dynamic writing.

Also, storing all results in memory might be problematic if there are millions. Let me use a two-pass approach: first count, then output.

But two-pass has the same iteration cost. Better: use printf directly.

Actually, for large outputs, I should use fwrite with a large buffer. Let me use setbuf to set a large stdout buffer.

Let me revise: instead of the custom buffer, use setvbuf with a large buffer and printf.

Actually the simplest: use cout with sync_with_stdio(false) for fast output.

Let me also reconsider storing all results. If there are 10M tets, that's 10M × 48 bytes = 480MB. With 127GB RAM, fine. But output of 10M lines × ~70 chars = 700MB text. With printf, that's maybe 10-30 seconds. With fast binary-like output it's faster.

For now, let me use a direct approach with printf and a large setvbuf.

Let me write the final, clean code now. I'll keep it simple and not worry too much about the output speed - if the number of tets is reasonable (< 1M), standard output is fine. For massive counts, the bottleneck is writing anyway.

One more thing I need to verify: the correctness of the rotation matrix computation.

Let me verify R1 analytically:
R1 maps canonical v0c → t1_0, v1c → t1_1, v2c → t1_2, v3c → t1_3.

Canonical tet has v0c along +z. T1 has t1_0 = (-r,-r,-r) along (-1,-1,-1) direction. 
Canonical v1c is in the yz-plane (x=0). T1's t1_1 = (r,r,-r) is not in any coordinate plane.

This doesn't give obvious Euler angles, but as long as R1 is a valid rotation matrix (det=1, orthogonal), the Euler angle extraction works.

Let me verify det(R1) = 1 numerically (for e=1):
det(B) = -√2/2 ≈ -0.7071 (computed earlier)
det(A_T1) = -16r³ = -16*(1/(2√2))³ = -16/(8*2√2) = -16/(16√2) = -1/√2 ≈ -0.7071
det(R1) = det(A_T1)/det(B) = (-1/√2)/(-√2/2) = (1/√2)*(2/√2) = 2/2 = 1 ✓

For R2 (with swapped t2_2,t2_3):
det(A_T2 swapped) = -det(A_T2) = -(16r³) = -1/√2 (for e=1)
det(R2) = (-1/√2)/(-√2/2) = 1 ✓

Both are proper rotations.

Now let me verify orthogonality. R = A*B^{-1}.
B is NOT orthogonal (since the canonical tet edges are not orthogonal). So B^{-1} ≠ B^T.
But R should still be orthogonal since it maps regular tet vertices to regular tet vertices.

Proof: Let V = [v0c|v1c|v2c|v3c] (4 cols) and T = [t0|t1|t2|t3] (4 cols, using proper assignment).
We have R*V = T (column by column).
For any two canonical vertices vi,vj: |R*vi - R*vj|² = |ti-tj|² = e² = |vi-vj|² (since both are edge 1).
Since R preserves all pairwise distances, R is an isometry. Combined with det(R)=1, it's a proper rotation. ✓

Great, so R1 and R2 are valid rotation matrices. The Euler angle extraction will give valid angles.

Now let me write the complete final code. I'll add OpenMP for parallelism.

Actually, one more issue: the containment check uses a tolerance eps=1e-7. For very small containers (edge ≈ e), a tet might be nearly touching the boundary. The eps should be small enough not to exclude valid placements but large enough to avoid numerical issues.

For now, eps=1e-7 seems fine for double precision (which has ~15 significant digits).

Also: for the convex hull, I should use eps=1e-9 for the coplanar check (vertices exactly on the face are not counted as being on one side). Let me use 1e-8 in the hull building.

Let me now write the FINAL code. This is taking too long, so I'll just write it cleanly.

Here are the key insights summarized:
1. FCC lattice with step = e/√2
2. Two tet types per lattice point: T1 and T2
3. T1 center at (u+0.5, v+0.5, w+0.5)*step
4. T2 center at (u+0.5, v+0.5, w-0.5)*step
5. Both are proper rotations of the canonical tet
6. Containment check using convex hull half-spaces

The code is correct. Let me finalize it.

Actually wait - I want to triple check one thing. Is it possible that T1 at some Q and T2 at some other Q' produce the same physical tetrahedron (same 4 vertex positions)?

T1 at Q: {Q, Q+(1,1,0)s, Q+(1,0,1)s, Q+(0,1,1)s}
T2 at Q': {Q', Q'+(1,1,0)s, Q'+(1,0,-1)s, Q'+(0,1,-1)s}

For these to be equal: {Q, Q+A_1, Q+E_1, Q+I_1} = {Q', Q'+A_2, Q'+F_2, Q'+J_2} 
(where subscripts 1 and 2 denote T1 and T2 offsets; A_1=A_2=A=(1,1,0)s).

One of Q, Q+A_1, Q+E_1, Q+I_1 must equal Q'.
If Q' = Q: then {A,E,I} offsets would need to equal {A,F,J} → need E=F and I=J → (1,0,1)=(-1...) no, E=(1,0,1)s ≠ F=(1,0,-1)s. ✗
If Q' = Q+A: we showed earlier that T1 at Q ≠ T2 at Q+A because:
  T2 at Q+A = {Q+A, Q+2A, Q+A+F, Q+A+J}
  For this to equal T1 at Q = {Q, Q+A, Q+E, Q+I}: need Q ∈ {Q+A, Q+2A, Q+A+F, Q+A+J}.
  Q = Q+A → A=0 ✗. Q = Q+2A → 2A=0 ✗. Q = Q+A+F → A+F=(2,1,-1)s ≠ 0 ✗. Q = Q+A+J → A+J=(1,2,-1)s ≠ 0 ✗. ✗
If Q' = Q+E: T2 at Q+E = {Q+E, Q+E+A, Q+E+F, Q+E+J}. For T1 at Q = {Q, Q+A, Q+E, Q+I}:
  Need Q ∈ {Q+E+A, Q+E+F, Q+E+J} (since Q+E is already in T1).
  Q = Q+E+A → E+A=(2,1,1)s ≠ 0 ✗. Q = Q+E+F → E+F=(2,0,0)s ≠ 0 ✗. Q = Q+E+J → E+J=(1,1,0)s=A ≠ 0 ✗. ✗
If Q' = Q+I: similarly fail.

So no double counting between T1 and T2. ✓

Also I should verify: no double counting within T1 tets (different Q1 ≠ Q2 give different T1 tets).
T1 at Q1 has Q1 as a vertex. T1 at Q2 has Q2 as a vertex. If they're the same tet, their vertex sets are equal. Q1 must be one of {Q2, Q2+A, Q2+E, Q2+I}. If Q1=Q2+A: T1 at Q1 = {Q2+A, Q2+2A, Q2+A+E, Q2+A+I}. For this to equal T1 at Q2 = {Q2, Q2+A, Q2+E, Q2+I}: need Q2 ∈ {Q2+2A, Q2+A+E, Q2+A+I} → 2A=0 or A+E=0 or A+I=0 → none true. ✗ Similarly for other cases. ✓ No T1 double counting. ✓

Great, the enumeration is correct.

Now for the final concern: do T1+T2 at all FCC points cover ALL tetrahedra in the tet-oct honeycomb?

From the analysis at origin: all 8 tets containing origin are covered by T1 or T2 at some vertex.
By lattice symmetry, the same holds for any FCC point. ✓
And we showed no double-counting. ✓
The honeycomb has exactly 2 tets per FCC point (primitive cell). ✓
T1+T2 gives exactly 2 tets per FCC point. ✓
Coverage is complete. ✓

The code is correct. Let me finalize.

```cpp
#include <cstdio>
#include <vector>
#include <array>
#include <cmath>
#include <algorithm>

using namespace std;
typedef array<double,3> V3;
typedef array<array<double,3>,3> M3;

// Vector math
inline V3 add(V3 a,V3 b){return{a[0]+b[0],a[1]+b[1],a[2]+b[2]};}
inline V3 sub(V3 a,V3 b){return{a[0]-b[0],a[1]-b[1],a[2]-b[2]};}
inline V3 scl(double s,V3 a){return{s*a[0],s*a[1],s*a[2]};}
inline double dot(V3 a,V3 b){return a[0]*b[0]+a[1]*b[1]+a[2]*b[2];}
inline V3 crs(V3 a,V3 b){return{a[1]*b[2]-a[2]*b[1],a[2]*b[0]-a[0]*b[2],a[0]*b[1]-a[1]*b[0]};}
inline double nrm(V3 a){return sqrt(dot(a,a));}
inline V3 nml(V3 a){double n=nrm(a);return n<1e-14?V3{0,0,0}:scl(1/n,a);}

// Matrix math
M3 mmul(M3 a,M3 b){
    M3 r{};
    for(int i=0;i<3;i++)for(int j=0;j<3;j++)for(int k=0;k<3;k++)r[i][j]+=a[i][k]*b[k][j];
    return r;
}
double det(M3& m){
    return m[0][0]*(m[1][1]*m[2][2]-m[1][2]*m[2][1])
          -m[0][1]*(m[1][0]*m[2][2]-m[1][2]*m[2][0])
          +m[0][2]*(m[1][0]*m[2][1]-m[1][1]*m[2][0]);
}
M3 inv(M3 m){
    double d=det(m);
    M3 r;
    r[0][0]=(m[1][1]*m[2][2]-m[1][2]*m[2][1])/d;
    r[0][1]=(m[0][2]*m[2][1]-m[0][1]*m[2][2])/d;
    r[0][2]=(m[0][1]*m[1][2]-m[0][2]*m[1][1])/d;
    r[1][0]=(m[1][2]*m[2][0]-m[1][0]*m[2][2])/d;
    r[1][1]=(m[0][0]*m[2][2]-m[0][2]*m[2][0])/d;
    r[1][2]=(m[0][2]*m[1][0]-m[0][0]*m[1][2])/d;
    r[2][0]=(m[1][0]*m[2][1]-m[1][1]*m[2][0])/d;
    r[2][1]=(m[0][1]*m[2][0]-m[0][0]*m[2][1])/d;
    r[2][2]=(m[0][0]*m[1][1]-m[0][1]*m[1][0])/d;
    return r;
}

array<double,3> toEuler(M3 R){
    double ry=asin(max(-1.0,min(1.0,-R[2][0])));
    double cy=cos(ry),rx,rz;
    if(fabs(cy)>1e-7){
        rx=atan2(R[2][1]/cy,R[2][2]/cy);
        rz=atan2(R[1][0]/cy,R[0][0]/cy);
    }else{
        rx=0;
        rz=atan2(-R[0][1],R[1][1]);
    }
    return{rx,ry,rz};
}

M3 buildRot(double e,V3 t0,V3 t1,V3 t2,V3 t3){
    const double s3=sqrt(3.0),s6=sqrt(6.0);
    V3 v0={0,0,e*s6/4};
    V3 v1={0,e/s3,-e*s6/12};
    V3 v2={-e/2,-e/(2*s3),-e*s6/12};
    V3 v3={e/2,-e/(2*s3),-e*s6/12};
    V3 b1=sub(v1,v0),b2=sub(v2,v0),b3=sub(v3,v0);
    M3 B={{{b1[0],b2[0],b3[0]},{b1[1],b2[1],b3[1]},{b1[2],b2[2],b3[2]}}};
    V3 a1=sub(t1,t0),a2=sub(t2,t0),a3=sub(t3,t0);
    M3 A={{{a1[0],a2[0],a3[0]},{a1[1],a2[1],a3[1]},{a1[2],a2[2],a3[2]}}};
    return mmul(A,inv(B));
}

struct HS{V3 n;double d;};

vector<HS> buildHull(const vector<V3>& pts){
    int n=pts.size();
    V3 cen={0,0,0};
    for(auto& p:pts){cen[0]+=p[0];cen[1]+=p[1];cen[2]+=p[2];}
    cen[0]/=n;cen[1]/=n;cen[2]/=n;
    vector<HS> hs;
    for(int i=0;i<n;i++)
    for(int j=i+1;j<n;j++)
    for(int k=j+1;k<n;k++){
        V3 nn=nml(crs(sub(pts[j],pts[i]),sub(pts[k],pts[i])));
        if(nrm(nn)<0.5)continue;
        double di=dot(nn,pts[i]);
        bool ok=true;int side=0;
        for(int l=0;l<n&&ok;l++){
            if(l==i||l==j||l==k)continue;
            double v=dot(nn,pts[l])-di;
            if(fabs(v)<1e-9)continue;
            int s=(v>0)?1:-1;
            if(!side)side=s;
            else if(s!=side)ok=false;
        }
        if(!ok)continue;
        if(dot(nn,cen)<di){nn=scl(-1,nn);di=-di;}
        bool dup=false;
        for(auto& h:hs)
            if(fabs(dot(h.n,nn)-1)<1e-6&&fabs(h.d-di)<1e-6){dup=true;break;}
        if(!dup)hs.push_back({nn,di});
    }
    return hs;
}

inline bool inH(const vector<HS>& hs,const V3& p,double eps=1e-7){
    for(auto& h:hs)if(dot(h.n,p)<h.d-eps)return false;
    return true;
}

static char buf[1<<26];
static int bp=0;

void flush(){fwrite(buf,1,bp,stdout);bp=0;}

void writeD(double x){
    char tmp[32];
    int n=sprintf(tmp,"%.10f",x);
    if(bp+n>(1<<26)-100)flush();
    for(int i=0;i<n;i++)buf[bp++]=tmp[i];
}

void writeI(long long x){
    char tmp[32];
    int n=sprintf(tmp,"%lld",x);
    if(bp+n>(1<<26)-100)flush();
    for(int i=0;i<n;i++)buf[bp++]=tmp[i];
}

void writeC(char c){
    if(bp>=(1<<26)-100)flush();
    buf[bp++]=c;
}

int main(){
    int V;double e;
    scanf("%d %lf",&V,&e);
    vector<V3> pts(V);
    for(int i=0;i<V;i++)scanf("%lf %lf %lf",&pts[i][0],&pts[i][1],&pts[i][2]);
    
    if(V<4){printf("0\n");return 0;}
    
    auto hs=buildHull(pts);
    if(hs.empty()){printf("0\n");return 0;}
    
    V3 lo={1e18,1e18,1e18},hi={-1e18,-1e18,-1e18};
    for(auto& p:pts)
        for(int d=0;d<3;d++){lo[d]=min(lo[d],p[d]);hi[d]=max(hi[d],p[d]);}
    
    const double S2=sqrt(2.0);
    double step=e/S2,r=step*0.5;
    
    // T1 centered verts: {(-r,-r,-r),(r,r,-r),(r,-r,r),(-r,r,r)}
    V3 T1[4]={{-r,-r,-r},{r,r,-r},{r,-r,r},{-r,r,r}};
    // T2 centered verts: {(-r,-r,r),(r,r,r),(r,-r,-r),(-r,r,-r)}
    // swap last two for proper rotation
    V3 T2[4]={{-r,-r,r},{r,r,r},{r,-r,-r},{-r,r,-r}};
    
    M3 R1=buildRot(e,T1[0],T1[1],T1[2],T1[3]);
    M3 R2=buildRot(e,T2[0],T2[1],T2[3],T2[2]); // swap 2,3
    
    auto eu1=toEuler(R1);
    auto eu2=toEuler(R2);
    
    int umin=(int)floor(lo[0]/step)-2,umax=(int)ceil(hi[0]/step)+2;
    int vmin=(int)floor(lo[1]/step)-2,vmax=(int)ceil(hi[1]/step)+2;
    int wmin=(int)floor(lo[2]/step)-2,wmax=(int)ceil(hi[2]/step)+2;
    
    struct Tet{float cx,cy,cz;int type;};
    vector<Tet> tets;
    tets.reserve(1<<20);
    
    for(int u=umin;u<=umax;u++){
        double qu=u*step;
        for(int v=vmin;v<=vmax;v++){
            double qv=v*step;
            for(int w=wmin;w<=wmax;w++){
                if(((u+v+w)&1))continue;
                double qw=w*step;
                
                // T1: verts at Q, Q+(1,1,0)s, Q+(1,0,1)s, Q+(0,1,1)s
                {
                    V3 p0={qu,qv,qw};
                    V3 p1={qu+step,qv+step,qw};
                    V3 p2={qu+step,qv,qw+step};
                    V3 p3={qu,qv+step,qw+step};
                    if(inH(hs,p0)&&inH(hs,p1)&&inH(hs,p2)&&inH(hs,p3))
                        tets.push_back({(float)(qu+r),(float)(qv+r),(float)(qw+r),0});
                }
                
                // T2: verts at Q, Q+(1,1,0)s, Q+(1,0,-1)s, Q+(0,1,-1)s
                {
                    V3 p0={qu,qv,qw};
                    V3 p1={qu+step,qv+step,qw};
                    V3 p2={qu+step,qv,qw-step};
                    V3 p3={qu,qv+step,qw-step};
                    if(inH(hs,p0)&&inH(hs,p1)&&inH(hs,p2)&&inH(hs,p3))
                        tets.push_back({(float)(qu+r),(float)(qv+r),(float)(qw-r),1});
                }
            }
        }
    }
    
    writeI(tets.size());
    writeC('\n');
    
    for(auto& t:tets){
        auto& eu=(t.type==0)?eu1:eu2;
        writeD(t.cx);writeC(' ');
        writeD(t.cy);writeC(' ');
        writeD(t.cz);writeC(' ');
        writeD(eu[0]);writeC(' ');
        writeD(eu[1]);writeC(' ');
        writeD(eu[2]);writeC('\n');
    }
    flush();
    
    return 0;
}
```

Hmm, I used `float` for the center coordinates but should use `double` for precision. Let me fix that.

Also, I realize I should verify the rotation is correct. Let me think about what happens for the canonical tet with Euler angles (0,0,0):
R(0,0,0) = identity. So v_i = center + I * v_ic = center + v_ic.
The 4 vertices would be at:
v0 = center + (0, 0, e*sqrt(6)/4)
v1 = center + (0, e/sqrt(3), -e*sqrt(6)/12)
v2 = center + (-e/2, -e/(2*sqrt(3)), -e*sqrt(6)/12)
v3 = center + (e/2, -e/(2*sqrt(3)), -e*sqrt(6)/12)

For T1 (eu1 angles), the vertices should be:
v0 = center + R1 * v0c = center + t1_0 = center + (-r,-r,-r)
v1 = center + t1_1 = center + (r,r,-r)
v2 = center + t1_2 = center + (r,-r,r)
v3 = center + t1_3 = center + (-r,r,r)

where center = Q + (r,r,r) for T1.
So the actual vertices are:
v0 = Q + (r,r,r) + (-r,-r,-r) = Q
v1 = Q + (r,r,r) + (r,r,-r) = Q + (2r,2r,0) = Q + (step,step,0) [since 2r=step] ✓
v2 = Q + (r,r,r) + (r,-r,r) = Q + (2r,0,2r) = Q + (step,0,step) ✓
v3 = Q + (r,r,r) + (-r,r,r) = Q + (0,2r,2r) = Q + (0,step,step) ✓



For T2 (eu2 angles), center = Q + (r,r,-r):
v0 = Q + (r,r,-r) + (-r,-r,r) = Q
v1 = Q + (r,r,-r) + (r,r,r) = Q + (2r,2r,0) = Q + (step,step,0) ✓
v2 = Q + (r,r,-r) + (r,-r,-r) = Q + (2r,0,-2r) = Q + (step,0,-step) ✓
v3 = Q + (r,r,-r) + (-r,r,-r) = Q + (0,2r,-2r) = Q + (0,step,-step) ✓

Everything checks out. The vertices in my T2 centered template map to the correct positions.

But wait: I'm using buildRot(e, T2[0], T2[1], T2[3], T2[2]) (swap T2[2] and T2[3]).
This means: R2 maps v0c→T2[0], v1c→T2[1], v2c→T2[3], v3c→T2[2].

So the actual tet (using R2) has vertices at:
- center + R2*v0c = center + T2[0] = center + (-r,-r,r)
- center + R2*v1c = center + T2[1] = center + (r,r,r)
- center + R2*v2c = center + T2[3] = center + (-r,r,-r)  [swapped]
- center + R2*v3c = center + T2[2] = center + (r,-r,-r)  [swapped]

But the CHECKER probably uses the Euler angles to reconstruct: R2 maps canonical→somewhere, and then:
- center + R2*v0c = center + (-r,-r,r) ← the actual vertex position depends on which canonical vertex maps where

If the checker has a DIFFERENT canonical tet ordering, the reconstructed vertices might be wrong.

Actually, this doesn't matter for correctness! The checker only needs to verify:
1. All 4 vertex positions are inside the container
2. No two tets overlap

If the checker reconstructs vertices as {center + R2*v0c, center + R2*v1c, center + R2*v2c, center + R2*v3c}, these will be {center+T2[0], center+T2[1], center+T2[3], center+T2[2]}, which is a permutation of {center+T2[0], center+T2[1], center+T2[2], center+T2[3]} - the same SET of 4 points! 

Wait, no. With my swapped assignment:
- center + R2*v0c = center + T2[0]
- center + R2*v1c = center + T2[1]
- center + R2*v2c = center + T2[3]  (T2[2] and T2[3] are swapped)
- center + R2*v3c = center + T2[2]

So the 4 vertices are {center+T2[0], center+T2[1], center+T2[3], center+T2[2]} = {center+T2[i] for i=0..3}. Same set of 4 points, just in a different order! ✓

For the CHECKER: it reconstructs 4 vertices as {center + R2*v_i for canonical v_i}. This gives the correct 4 positions (the same 4 points as the T2 tet at Q). ✓

Does it matter which order the checker checks them? For containment: checks each of 4 points - order doesn't matter. ✓ For non-overlap: checks if tet interiors intersect - this depends on the tet geometry (vertex positions), not their order. ✓

So my approach is correct.

BUT: the checker might use a DIFFERENT canonical tet (different v_i). In that case, center + checker_R2 * checker_v_i ≠ center + my_R2 * my_v_i (for the same Euler angles).

This is the fundamental issue. If the checker uses a different canonical tet, my Euler angles will give wrong vertex positions.

To work around this: the checker MUST verify that the 4 vertices form a valid regular tetrahedron (edge length e), are inside the container, and don't overlap other tets. But the "center + Euler angles" format implies a specific canonical tet.

I think the problem setter has a specific canonical in mind. Given they mention:
- Circumradius R ≈ 0.6124 (matching my canonical)
- Height h ≈ 0.8165

And common convention: apex along +z, base in xy-plane. My canonical v0=(0,0,R) is along +z. Seems natural.

For the Euler angle convention: ZYX is common. I'll use it.

Let me check: for the IDENTITY rotation (rx=ry=rz=0), R=I. Vertices would be at center ± {my canonical verts}. The tet is at:
v0 = center + (0, 0, R_circ) (apex at top)
v1 = center + (0, 1/√3, -r_in) (1/√3 ≈ 0.577, r_in ≈ 0.204)
v2 = center + (-0.5, -0.289, -0.204)
v3 = center + (0.5, -0.289, -0.204)

This is a "standard" regular tetrahedron with apex pointing up. Reasonable.

For T1 (Euler angles eu1): R1 rotates this standard tet to the T1 orientation. ✓

For T2 (eu2): similarly. ✓

I'm fairly confident my approach is correct. Let me finalize the code.

One more thing: for MASSIVE output, I should use a fast output method. Let me use a large output buffer with fwrite.

Here's my final code:

```cpp
#include <cstdio>
#include <cmath>
#include <vector>
#include <array>
#include <algorithm>

using namespace std;
typedef array<double,3> V3;
typedef array<array<double,3>,3> M3;

V3 add(V3 a,V3 b){return{a[0]+b[0],a[1]+b[1],a[2]+b[2]};}
V3 sub(V3 a,V3 b){return{a[0]-b[0],a[1]-b[1],a[2]-b[2]};}
V3 scl(double s,V3 a){return{s*a[0],s*a[1],s*a[2]};}
double dot(V3 a,V3 b){return a[0]*b[0]+a[1]*b[1]+a[2]*b[2];}
V3 crs(V3 a,V3 b){return{a[1]*b[2]-a[2]*b[1],a[2]*b[0]-a[0]*b[2],a[0]*b[1]-a[1]*b[0]};}
double nrm(V3 a){return sqrt(dot(a,a));}
V3 nml(V3 a){double n=nrm(a);return n<1e-14?V3{0,0,0}:scl(1/n,a);}

M3 mul(M3 a,M3 b){M3 r{};for(int i=0;i<3;i++)for(int j=0;j<3;j++)for(int k=0;k<3;k++)r[i][j]+=a[i][k]*b[k][j];return r;}
double det3(M3 m){return m[0][0]*(m[1][1]*m[2][2]-m[1][2]*m[2][1])-m[0][1]*(m[1][0]*m[2][2]-m[1][2]*m[2][0])+m[0][2]*(m[1][0]*m[2][1]-m[1][1]*m[2][0]);}
M3 inv3(M3 m){
    double d=det3(m);
    M3 r;
    r[0]={(m[1][1]*m[2][2]-m[1][2]*m[2][1])/d,(m[0][2]*m[2][1]-m[0][1]*m[2][2])/d,(m[0][1]*m[1][2]-m[0][2]*m[1][1])/d};
    r[1]={(m[1][2]*m[2][0]-m[1][0]*m[2][2])/d,(m[0][0]*m[2][2]-m[0][2]*m[2][0])/d,(m[0][2]*m[1][0]-m[0][0]*m[1][2])/d};
    r[2]={(m[1][0]*m[2][1]-m[1][1]*m[2][0])/d,(m[0][1]*m[2][0]-m[0][0]*m[2][1])/d,(m[0][0]*m[1][1]-m[0][1]*m[1][0])/d};
    return r;
}

array<double,3> euler(M3 R){
    double ry=asin(max(-1.0,min(1.0,-R[2][0])));
    double cy=cos(ry),rx,rz;
    if(fabs(cy)>1e-7){rx=atan2(R[2][1]/cy,R[2][2]/cy);rz=atan2(R[1][0]/cy,R[0][0]/cy);}
    else{rx=0;rz=atan2(-R[0][1],R[1][1]);}
    return{rx,ry,rz};
}

M3 rotMat(double e,V3 t0,V3 t1,V3 t2,V3 t3){
    double s3=sqrt(3.0),s6=sqrt(6.0);
    V3 v0={0,0,e*s6/4},v1={0,e/s3,-e*s6/12},v2={-e/2,-e/(2*s3),-e*s6/12},v3={e/2,-e/(2*s3),-e*s6/12};
    V3 b1=sub(v1,v0),b2=sub(v2,v0),b3=sub(v3,v0);
    M3 B={{{b1[0],b2[0],b3[0]},{b1[1],b2[1],b3[1]},{b1[2],b2[2],b3[2]}}};
    V3 a1=sub(t1,t0),a2=sub(t2,t0),a3=sub(t3,t0);
    M3 A={{{a1[0],a2[0],a3[0]},{a1[1],a2[1],a3[1]},{a1[2],a2[2],a3[2]}}};
    return mul(A,inv3(B));
}

struct HS{V3 n;double d;};

vector<HS> hull(vector<V3>& pts){
    int n=pts.size();
    V3 c={0,0,0};
    for(auto& p:pts){c[0]+=p[0];c[1]+=p[1];c[2]+=p[2];}
    c=scl(1.0/n,c);
    vector<HS> h;
    for(int i=0;i<n;i++)
    for(int j=i+1;j<n;j++)
    for(int k=j+1;k<n;k++){
        V3 nn=nml(crs(sub(pts[j],pts[i]),sub(pts[k],pts[i])));
        if(nrm(nn)<0.5)continue;
        double di=dot(nn,pts[i]);
        bool ok=true;int s=0;
        for(int l=0;l<n&&ok;l++){
            if(l==i||l==j||l==k)continue;
            double v=dot(nn,pts[l])-di;
            if(fabs(v)<1e-9)continue;
            int si=(v>0)?1:-1;
            if(!s)s=si;else if(s!=si)ok=false;
        }
        if(!ok)continue;
        if(dot(nn,c)<di){nn=scl(-1,nn);di=-di;}
        bool dup=false;
        for(auto& x:h)if(fabs(dot(x.n,nn)-1)<1e-6&&fabs(x.d-di)<1e-6){dup=true;break;}
        if(!dup)h.push_back({nn,di});
    }
    return h;
}

inline bool in(const vector<HS>& h,const V3& p,double eps=1e-7){
    for(auto& x:h)if(dot(x.n,p)<x.d-eps)return false;
    return true;
}

// Fast output buffer
static char obuf[1<<25];
static int opos=0;
void oflush(){fwrite(obuf,1,opos,stdout);opos=0;}
void ochar(char c){if(opos>=(1<<25)-200)oflush();obuf[opos++]=c;}
void odbl(double x){char t[32];int n=sprintf(t,"%.10f",x);for(int i=0;i<n;i++)ochar(t[i]);}
void oint(long long x){char t[32];int n=sprintf(t,"%lld",x);for(int i=0;i<n;i++)ochar(t[i]);}

int main(){
    int V;double e;
    scanf("%d %lf",&V,&e);
    vector<V3> pts(V);
    for(int i=0;i<V;i++)scanf("%lf %lf %lf",&pts[i][0],&pts[i][1],&pts[i][2]);
    
    if(V<4){puts("0");return 0;}
    
    auto hs=hull(pts);
    if(hs.empty()){puts("0");return 0;}
    
    V3 lo={1e18,1e18,1e18},hi={-1e18,-1e18,-1e18};
    for(auto& p:pts)for(int d=0;d<3;d++){lo[d]=min(lo[d],p[d]);hi[d]=max(hi[d],p[d]);}
    
    double S2=sqrt(2.0),step=e/S2,r=step*0.5;
    
    // T1 centered: {(-r,-r,-r),(r,r,-r),(r,-r,r),(-r,r,r)}
    V3 C1[4]={{-r,-r,-r},{r,r,-r},{r,-r,r},{-r,r,r}};
    // T2 centered: {(-r,-r,r),(r,r,r),(r,-r,-r),(-r,r,-r)}
    // Use indices 0,1,3,2 to get proper rotation
    V3 C2[4]={{-r,-r,r},{r,r,r},{r,-r,-r},{-r,r,-r}};
    
    M3 R1=rotMat(e,C1[0],C1[1],C1[2],C1[3]);
    M3 R2=rotMat(e,C2[0],C2[1],C2[3],C2[2]);
    
    auto eu1=euler(R1);
    auto eu2=euler(R2);
    
    int umin=(int)floor(lo[0]/step)-2,umax=(int)ceil(hi[0]/step)+2;
    int vmin=(int)floor(lo[1]/step)-2,vmax=(int)ceil(hi[1]/step)+2;
    int wmin=(int)floor(lo[2]/step)-2,wmax=(int)ceil(hi[2]/step)+2;
    
    // Count pass
    long long cnt=0;
    
    // We'll do two passes for large output: or store in memory
    // For simplicity: store centers and types
    struct Rec{double x,y,z;int t;};
    vector<Rec> recs;
    recs.reserve(1<<16);
    
    for(int u=umin;u<=umax;u++){
        double qu=u*step;
        for(int v=vmin;v<=vmax;v++){
            double qv=v*step;
            for(int w=wmin;w<=wmax;w++){
                if((u+v+w)&1)continue;
                double qw=w*step;
                
                // T1
                {
                    V3 p0={qu,qv,qw};
                    V3 p1={qu+step,qv+step,qw};
                    V3 p2={qu+step,qv,qw+step};
                    V3 p3={qu,qv+step,qw+step};
                    if(in(hs,p0)&&in(hs,p1)&&in(hs,p2)&&in(hs,p3))
                        recs.push_back({qu+r,qv+r,qw+r,0});
                }
                
                // T2
                {
                    V3 p0={qu,qv,qw};
                    V3 p1={qu+step,qv+step,qw};
                    V3 p2={qu+step,qv,qw-step};
                    V3 p3={qu,qv+step,qw-step};
                    if(in(hs,p0)&&in(hs,p1)&&in(hs,p2)&&in(hs,p3))
                        recs.push_back({qu+r,qv+r,qw-r,1});
                }
            }
        }
    }
    
    oint((long long)recs.size());ochar('\n');
    for(auto& r:recs){
        auto& eu=(r.t==0)?eu1:eu2;
        odbl(r.x);ochar(' ');odbl(r.y);ochar(' ');odbl(r.z);ochar(' ');
        odbl(eu[0]);ochar(' ');odbl(eu[1]);ochar(' ');odbl(eu[2]);ochar('\n');
    }
    oflush();
    
    return 0;
}
```

This looks good. Let me review one more time:

1. Parse V and edge_length correctly ✓
2. Build convex hull from V vertices ✓
3. FCC lattice with step = e/√2 ✓
4. Two tet types: T1 and T2 ✓
5. Containment check for all 4 vertices ✓
6. Output count and centers+Euler angles ✓

One potential issue: the `(u+v+w)&1` check uses bitwise AND, which assumes the values are non-negative. For negative u,v,w, this could be wrong!

In C++, `(-3)&1 = 1` (assuming two's complement, which it is). And `-3 % 2 = -1` in C++. So `(u+v+w)&1` correctly gives the parity (0 for even, 1 for odd) even for negative numbers in two's complement. ✓

Actually wait: `(-1)&1 = 1` (correct, since -1 is odd) and `(-2)&1 = 0` (correct, -2 is even). ✓ So the check is correct.

Another issue: the output buffer size is 1<<25 = 32MB. For large outputs, we flush it multiple times. The `ochar`, `odbl`, `oint` functions check for capacity and flush when needed. ✓

But: storing all results in memory (vector<Rec>) might be a problem for very large outputs (say 100M records × 24 bytes = 2.4GB). Let me stream the output instead.

For streaming, I need to know the count before writing. So I'll either:
a) Two-pass: count, then output (double the compute time)
b) Write to a temp buffer in memory (fine for typical sizes)
c) Use a two-step approach: collect while outputting count later

For now, let me use the in-memory approach but handle large sizes by streaming directly.

Actually, for streaming I can:
1. Write all results to a temp file
2. Read count from result size
3. Output count followed by temp file contents

But file I/O complicates things. Let me just use in-memory but with a smarter reservation:

```cpp
recs.reserve(min(est_tets, (long long)1<<24)); // cap at 16M
```

```cpp
bool use_twopass = (bb_vol > (long long)1<<26); // >64M lattice points
if(use_twopass){
    // First pass: count
    long long cnt = 0;
    for(int u...) {
        // count only

    }

    }
} else {

```

This doubles the computation but halves the memory. For very large cases this is necessary.

Let me implement this cleanly. The two-pass approach:

```cpp
auto checkT1 = [&](int u,int v,int w)->bool{
    double qu=u*step,qv=v*step,qw=w*step;
    V3 p0={qu,qv,qw},p1={qu+step,qv+step,qw},p2={qu+step,qv,qw+step},p3={qu,qv+step,qw+step};
    return in(hs,p0)&&in(hs,p1)&&in(hs,p2)&&in(hs,p3);
};
auto checkT2 = [&](int u,int v,int w)->bool{
    double qu=u*step,qv=v*step,qw=w*step;
    V3 p0={qu,qv,qw},p1={qu+step,qv+step,qw},p2={qu+step,qv,qw-step},p3={qu,qv+step,qw-step};
    return in(hs,p0)&&in(hs,p1)&&in(hs,p2)&&in(hs,p3);
};

// Count pass
long long cnt=0;
for(int u=umin;u<=umax;u++)
    for(int v=vmin;v<=vmax;v++)
        for(int w=wmin;w<=wmax;w++){
            if((u+v+w)&1)continue;
            if(checkT1(u,v,w))cnt++;
            if(checkT2(u,v,w))cnt++;
        }

oint(cnt);ochar('\n');

// Output pass
for(int u=umin;u<=umax;u++){
    double qu=u*step;
    for(int v=vmin;v<=vmax;v++){
        double qv=v*step;
        for(int w=wmin;w<=wmax;w++){
            if((u+v+w)&1)continue;
            double qw=w*step;
            if(checkT1(u,v,w)){
                odbl(qu+r);ochar(' ');odbl(qv+r);ochar(' ');odbl(qw+r);ochar(' ');
                odbl(eu1[0]);ochar(' ');odbl(eu1[1]);ochar(' ');odbl(eu1[2]);ochar('\n');
            }
            if(checkT2(u,v,w)){
                odbl(qu+r);ochar(' ');odbl(qv+r);ochar(' ');odbl(qw-r);ochar(' ');
                odbl(eu2[0]);ochar(' ');odbl(eu2[1]);ochar(' ');odbl(eu2[2]);ochar('\n');
            }
        }
    }
}
```

This always does two passes. For the "ludicrous scale" problem, this is fine: 2 × compute_time.

Actually, wait. With 64 cores and OpenMP, I can do the counting pass in parallel, then the output pass sequentially (since output must be in order, or... actually order doesn't matter as long as count matches).

Let me add OpenMP for the counting pass (using reduction):

```cpp
#ifdef _OPENMP
#pragma omp parallel for reduction(+:cnt) schedule(dynamic,4) collapse(2)
#endif
for(int u=umin;u<=umax;u++)
    for(int v=vmin;v<=vmax;v++){
        for(int w=wmin;w<=wmax;w++){
            if((u+v+w)&1)continue;
            if(checkT1(u,v,w))cnt++;
            if(checkT2(u,v,w))cnt++;
        }
    }
```

And for the output pass, I can also parallelize with per-thread buffers.
